There are\\n69:     no implicit dependencies between numbered migrations - the numbering is\\n70:     merely a convention to aid file listing. Every new numbered migration\\n71:     has a declared dependency to the previous number, meaning that VCS\\n72:     branch merges can be detected and resolved.\\n73: \\n74:     Migrations files can be marked as replacing another set of migrations -\\n75:     this is to support the \\\"squash\\\" feature. The graph handler isn't\\n76:     responsible for these; instead, the code to load them in here should\\n77:     examine the migration files and if the replaced migrations are all either\\n78:     unapplied or not present, it should ignore the replaced ones, load in just\\n79:     the replacing migration, and repoint any dependencies that pointed to the\\n80:     replaced migrations to point to the replacing one.\\n81: \\n82:     A node should be a tuple: (app_path, migration_name). The tree\\n83:     special-cases things within an app - namely, root nodes and leaf nodes\\n84:     ignore dependencies to other apps.\\n85:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n86: \\n87:     def __init__(self):\\n88:         self.node_map = {}\\n89:         self.nodes = {}\\n90: \\n91:     def add_node(self, key, migration):\\n92:         assert key not in self.node_map\\n93:         node = Node(key)\\n94:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n95:         self.nodes[key] = migration\\n96: \\n97:     def add_dummy_node(self, key, origin, error_message):\\n98:         node = DummyNode(key, origin, error_message)\\n99:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n100:         self.nodes[key] = None\\n101: \\n102:     def add_dependency(self, migration, child, parent, skip_validation=False):\\n103:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n104:         This may create dummy nodes if they don't yet exist. Any\\n128:         dependencies that were referencing them are changed to reference the\\n129:         `replacement` node instead.\\n130:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n131:         # Cast list of replaced keys to set to speed up lookup later.\\n132:         replaced = set(replaced)\\n133:         try:\\n134:             replacement_node = self.node_map[replacement]\\n135:         except KeyError as err:\\n136:             raise NodeNotFoundError(\\n137:                 \\\"Unable to find replacement node %r. It was either never added\\\"\\n138:                 \\\" to the migration graph, or has been removed.\\\" % (replacement,),\\n139:                 replacement,\\n140:             ) from err\\n141:         for replaced_key in replaced:\\n142:             self.nodes.pop(replaced_key, None)\\n143:             replaced_node = self.node_map.pop(replaced_key, None)\\n144:             if replaced_node:\\n145:                 for child in replaced_node.children:\\n146:                     child.parents.remove(replaced_node)\\n147:                     # We don't want to create dependencies between the replaced\\n148:                     # node and the replacement node as this would lead to\\n149:                     # self-referencing on the replacement node at a later\\n150:                     # iteration.\\n151:                     if child.key not in replaced:\\n152:                         replacement_node.add_child(child)\\n153:                         child.add_parent(replacement_node)\\n154:                 for parent in replaced_node.parents:\\n155:                     parent.children.remove(replaced_node)\\n156:                     # Again, to avoid self-referencing.\\n157:                     if parent.key not in replaced:\\n158:                         replacement_node.add_parent(parent)\\n159:                         parent.add_child(replacement_node)\\n160: \\n161:     def remove_replacement_node(self, replacement, replaced):\\n162:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n163:         The inverse operation to `remove_replaced_nodes`. Almost. Remove the\\n164:         replacement node `replacement` and remap its child nodes to `replaced`\\n165:         - the list of nodes it would have replaced. Don't remap its parent\\n166:         nodes as they are expected to be correct already.\\n167:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n168:         self.nodes.pop(replacement, None)\\n169:         try:\\n170:             replacement_node = self.node_map.pop(replacement)\\n171:         except KeyError as err:\\n172:             raise NodeNotFoundError(\\n173:                 \\\"Unable to remove replacement node %r. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_016F4yzHsiidpBXh7Kr3rrWk","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: class MigrationOptimizer:\\n2:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n3:     Power the optimization process, where you provide a list of Operations\\n4:     and you are returned a list of equal or shorter length - operations\\n5:     are merged into one if possible.\\n6: \\n7:     For example, a CreateModel and an AddField can be optimized into a\\n8:     new CreateModel, and CreateModel and DeleteModel can be optimized into\\n9:     nothing.\\n10:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n11: \\n12:     def optimize(self, operations, app_label):\\n13:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n14:         Main optimization entry point. Pass in a list of Operation instances,\\n15:         get out a new list of Operation instances.\\n16: \\n17:         Unfortunately, due to the scope of the optimization (two combinable\\n18:         operations might be separated by several hundred others), this can't be\\n19:         done as a peephole optimization with checks/output implemented on\\n20:         the Operations themselves; instead, the optimizer looks at each\\n21:         individual operation and scans forwards in the list to see if there\\n22:         are any matches, stopping at boundaries - operations which can't\\n23:         be optimized over (RunSQL, operations on the same field/model, etc.)\\n24: \\n25:         The inner loop is run until the starting list is the same as the result\\n26:         list, and then the result is returned. This means that operation\\n27:         optimization must be stable and always return an equal or shorter list.\\n28:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n29:         # Internal tracking variable for test assertions about # squashing compliance system is implemented across multiple interconnected modules in the django/db/migrations package and management commands.\\n\\n**Squash Migration Generator**: The squashmigrations command (django/core/management/commands/squashmigrations.py:Command.handle) is the primary entry point for generating squashed migrations. It collects all migration operations between a start and end migration, optimizes them using MigrationOptimizer, and creates a new migration instance with a replaces attribute that lists all replaced migrations. The command then writes the new migration file using MigrationWriter.\\n\\n**Replaced Migrations Tracking**: The Migration class (django/db/migrations/migration.py:Migration) defines a replaces attribute that lists migrations being replaced. The MigrationLoader (django/db/migrations/loader.py) manages replaced migration tracking through three key methods: (1) replace_migration() processes each replacing migration recursively and determines whether to apply the replacement or not based on whether all replaced migrations are either applied or unapplied; (2) _resolve_replaced_migration_keys() recursively resolves migration keys to find the ultimate migration targets; (3) all_replaced_applied() checks if all migrations in a replace chain have been applied. The MigrationRecorder (django/db/migrations/recorder.py:MigrationRecorder.record_applied and record_unapplied) tracks which migrations are in the applied state in the database. The MigrationExecutor (django/db/migrations/executor.py:MigrationExecutor.record_migration) records both the squashed migration and each of its replaced migrations when applied, and check_replacements() marks replacement migrations as applied when all their replaced migrations are applied.\\n\\n**Dependency Graph Validation**: The MigrationGraph (django/db/migrations/graph.py) implements critical validation logic: (1) validate_consistency() ensures no dummy nodes (representing missing/unresolved dependencies) remain in the graph after all migrations are loaded; (2) ensure_not_cyclic() uses a depth-first search algorithm to detect circular dependencies; (3) remove_replaced_nodes() updates the dependency graph by remapping all parent and child references from replaced migrations to the replacement migration while avoiding self-references; (4) remove_replacement_node() performs the inverse operation when a partially-applied squashed migration must be removed. The loader's build_graph() method calls these validation methods after adding all migrations to ensure consistency.\\n\\n**Squash Completeness Check**: The MigrationLoader.check_consistent_history() method validates that all applied migrations have their dependencies satisfied - if a migration is applied but its parent dependencies aren't, it raises InconsistentMigrationHistory. This check includes special handling for replaced migrations via all_replaced_applied() which allows skipping unapplied squashed migrations if all their replaced migrations are applied.\\n\\n**Supporting Components**: The MigrationOptimizer (django/db/migrations/optimizer.py:MigrationOptimizer.optimize) reduces the number of operations in squashed migrations by combining compatible operations. The MigrationWriter (django/db/migrations/writer.py:MigrationWriter.as_string) serializes the squashed migration with its replaces attribute into the migration file format. The optimizemigration command (django/core/management/commands/optimizemigration.py) allows further optimization of individual migrations. The exceptions module (django/db/migrations/exceptions.py) defines NodeNotFoundError, CircularDependencyError, and InconsistentMigrationHistory which are raised during validation failures.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":875,"cache_read_input_tokens":71652,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":875},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7d1860e6-2c62-42cb-9937-0601facb21e3","uuid":"45ae9499-de97-4847-aeca-51cd143ea303"}
